               \n                \n                 <span class=\"Z3988\" title=\"\">\n                                    </span>\n\n                \n                            </li>\n                </ol>\n    </div>\n\n    \n      <h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"app\"></a>Appendix A:  Automated Stage I procedure</h2>\n<p>\n          <a name=\"F8\"></a><div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F8.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-fig8_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F8.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. A.1</span></a><p>Example of time-delay estimations and confidence level from the automated procedure. The vertical grey dashed line represents the true value of the time delay. The blue diamonds correspond to the smallest absolute average residuals <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>r</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> returned by the automated procedure. The depth of the two minima <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> are represented by the number below each minimum. The colour bar indicates the microlensing variability <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#958;</i></span> (see text).</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=8&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n        </p>\n<p>If more time had been devoted to the visual inspection, we expect that more correctly estimated plausible time-delay estimations would have been classified as secure. After the TDC1, we developed an automated Stage I procedure. Its goal is to speed up and possibly improve the quality of the D3CS output by providing a range of reasonable initial time delays and associated confidence estimation. The following section describes technically how the time-delay and confidence estimation for this automated procedure are computed. </p>\n<h3 class=\"bold\">\n<a name=\"S14\"></a>Appendix A.1: Time-delay estimation</h3>\n<p>For each pair of curves, a bounded-optimal-knot spline (<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#R14\">Molinari et al. 2004</a>; <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#R23\">Tewes et al. 2013a</a>) <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>s</i>(<i>t</i>)</span> is fitted to one of the two light curves. The second light curve <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>l</i>(<i>t</i>)</span> is then shifted by an amount <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;t</i></span> in time and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;m</i></span> in magnitude. Thus, for a given observing epoch <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>t</i></span>, the value of the shifted light curve can be written as <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>l</i>(<i>t</i>&#8722;<i>&#948;t</i>)<sub><i>&#948;</i>m</sub></span>. For every value of the time and magnitude shifts, we select all the <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>N</i></span> points in the second light curve that overlap in time with the spline. For these points, we compute the residuals <span class=\"simple-math\">res<sub><i>n</i></sub></span> relative to the spline, i.e. the difference in magnitude between the points and the spline. The residual <span class=\"simple-math\">res<sub><i>n</i></sub></span> for point <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>n</i></span> is <a name=\"\"></a><span class=\"img-equation\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq67.png\"><span class=\"label-eq\">(A.1)</span></span>We then compute the average absolute residual <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>r</i>(<i>&#948;t,&#948;m</i>)</span> for every time and magnitude shift, i.e. <a name=\"\"></a><span class=\"img-equation\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq69.png\"><span class=\"label-eq\">(A.2)</span></span>\\newpage\\noindentThe possible presence of microlensing, assumed to be constant over an observing season, is handled in a very simple way. For each time shift <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span>, we apply independent magnitude shifts <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;</i><i>m</i><sub><i>j</i></sub>(<i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>)</span> to each season <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>j</i></span>. We define the residual curve <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>r</i></b> =  {<i>r</i><sub>1</sub>,<i>...</i>,<i>r</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>,<i>...</i>,<i>r</i><sub>T</sub>}</span> as the sum of the smallest average absolute residuals for each season <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>j</i></span>. The <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>i</i></span> index runs from 1 to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>T</i></span> and denotes the different time-delay values <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub>i</sub></span> we want to test. This translates into <a name=\"\"></a><span class=\"img-equation\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq77.png\"><span class=\"label-eq\">(A.3)</span></span>We define <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>r</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> as a local minimum in <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>r</i></b></span> if <a name=\"\"></a><span class=\"img-equation\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq79.png\"><span class=\"label-eq\">(A.4)</span></span>where we keep the absolute minimum in <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>r</i></b></span> as the final time-delay estimation. The <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>k</i></span> index running from 1 to 10 spans a range of <span class=\"simple-math\">&#177;</span>20 days around each tested value <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>r</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span>. Figure <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F8\">A.1</a> shows a typical residual curve <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>r</i></b></span> with the absolute minimum indicated as a coloured diamond and the true time delay indicated as a vertical dashed grey line. </p>\n<h3 class=\"bold\">\n<a name=\"S15\"></a>Appendix A.2: Confidence estimation</h3>\n<p>For each pair of curves, we compute three parameters related to the shape of the residual curve <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>r</i></b></span> that can be used to estimate the quality of the time-delay estimations:</p>\n<p>\n            <ul style=\"list-style-type: none;\">\n              <li>\n                1. \n                <p class=\"ligne\"> The number of local minima in <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>r</i></b></span>. </p>\n              </li>\n              <li>\n                2. \n                <p class=\"ligne\"> The depth of each minimum <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> and the absolute (i.e. the deepest) minimum <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i></span>, <a name=\"\"></a><span class=\"img-equation\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq82.png\"><span class=\"label-eq\">(A.5)</span></span>where <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i><sub><i>r</i></sub></span> is the standard deviation between the elements in <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>r</i></b></span>. Examples of values for <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> are indicated in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F8\">A.1</a> below the minima for time shifts <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;t</i> &#8771; &#8722;120</span> days and <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;t</i> &#8771;  + 80</span> days. </p>\n              </li>\n              <li>\n                3. \n                <p class=\"ligne\"> The total magnitude shift <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>&#948;m</i></b> =  {<i>&#948;</i><i>m</i><sub>1</sub>,<i>...</i><i>,&#948;</i><i>m</i><sub>T</sub>}</span> and the microlensing variability <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#958;</i>(<i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>,<b><i>&#948;m</i></b>)</span>, where we use the per season magnitude shifts <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;</i><i>m</i><sub><i>j</i></sub>(<i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>)</span> minimizing the average absolute residual <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>r</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> at each time shift <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span>, <a name=\"\"></a><span class=\"img-equation\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq88.png\"><span class=\"label-eq\">(A.6)</span></span>where <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#963;</i><sub><b><i>&#948;m</i></b></sub></span> is the standard deviation between the elements in <span class=\"simple-math\"><b><i>&#948;m</i></b></span>. In other words the quantity <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#958;</i>(<i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>,<b><i>&#948;m</i></b>)</span> is the difference between the sum of the magnitude shifts applied to each season at a given time shift <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#948;</i><i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> and the minimum of this sum on all time shifts. This quantity follows the colour code in the sidebar of Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F8\">A.1</a> and is equivalent to the season-to-season microlensing variations minimizing the residuals for a given time shift. The lower this quantity is, the smaller the impact of microlensing is. </p>\n              </li>\n            </ul>\n          </p>\n    \n  <h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"tabs\"></a>All Tables</h2>\n<div class=\"inset\"><div class=\"ligne\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/T1.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Table 1</span></a><p>D3CS classification of the TDC1 light curve pairs.</p>\n<div class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#T1\">In the text</a></div>\n</div></div>\n<h2 class=\"sec\">\n<a name=\"figs\"></a>All Figures</h2>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F1.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-fig1_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F1.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 1</span></a><p><i>Left</i><i> panel</i>: stacked histogram of the errors made by the visual time-delay estimation, for the secure and <tt>plausible D3CS </tt>samples. All the secure estimations are within the displayed range of errors of <span class=\"simple-math\">&#177; 20</span> days. Only <span class=\"simple-math\">2.6%</span> of the time delays in the plausible sample have an absolute error larger than 20 days. <i>Right panel</i>: absolute time-delay error made by D3CS as a function of the true delay for both samples.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=1&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F1\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F2.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-fig2_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F2.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 2</span></a><p>Cumulative evolution of the fraction of catastrophic outliers <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#1013;</i></span> (in percentage points) as a function of the number of time-delay estimations. Each black line (solid, dashed and dotted) represents a different subsample (see text for details). The coloured diamonds show the value of <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#1013;</i></span> for the D3CS combined samples; the corresponding number of estimations are indicated in parenthesis.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=2&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F2\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F3.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-fig3_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F3.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 3</span></a><p> Quantitative analysis of the discoverability of time delays through the extensive visual search with D3CS (Stage I) in the case of four-month observing seasons and a cadence of 3 days. In all panels, only tiles describing more than three light curve pairs are shown.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=5&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F5\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F6.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-fig6_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F6.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 6</span></a><p>Evolution of the TDC1 metrics per rung as a function of the fraction of estimations <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>f</i></span> for the spl-sec and sdi-sec samples. The plots are sorted by increasing values of the blind precision <span class=\"img-inline\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq38.png\"></span> (see text). Shaded regions represent the error on the metrics. Solid grey lines show the target values for the metrics as defined in the TDC1 paper. Dashed grey lines show the best possible value for each metric. The <i>bottom row </i>presents the non-cumulative evolution of the median of the true time delays <span class=\"simple-math\">| &#916;<i>t</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> |</span> in bins of ten estimations.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=6&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F6\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F7.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-fig7_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F7.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. 7</span></a><p>Evolution of the TDC1 metrics with the fraction of estimations sorted by increasing blind precision <span class=\"img-inline\"><img src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-eq38.png\"></span>, for the spl-sec and spl-secpla samples merging all rungs. The spl-secpla-cut sample has been cleaned a posteriori from the outliers in the spl-secpla sample. In doing so, we removed 29 curves from the spl-secpla sample. The shaded regions, the solid and dashed grey lines are the same as in Fig. <a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F6\">6</a>.</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=7&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F7\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n<div class=\"inset\"><table>\n<tr>\n<td valign=\"middle\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F8.html\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"thumbnail\" src=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15-fig8_small.jpg\"></a></td>\n<td class=\"img-txt\">\n<a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/F8.html\" target=\"_blank\"><span class=\"bold\">Fig. A.1</span></a><p>Example of time-delay estimations and confidence level from the automated procedure. The vertical grey dashed line represents the true value of the time delay. The blue diamonds correspond to the smallest absolute average residuals <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>r</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> returned by the automated procedure. The depth of the two minima <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#956;</i><sub><i>i</i></sub></span> are represented by the number below each minimum. The colour bar indicates the microlensing variability <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#958;</i></span> (see text).</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\"><a href=\"http://dexter.edpsciences.org/applet.php?pdf_id=8&amp;DOI=10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" target=\"DEXTER\">Open with DEXTER</a></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan=\"2\" class=\"in-txt\"><a href=\"/articles/aa/full_html/2016/01/aa26704-15/aa26704-15.html#F8\">In the text</a></td></tr>\n</table></div>\n</div>\n\n\r\n</div>\r\n\r\n    <div id=\"metrics-tabs\" data-doi=\"10.1051/0004-6361/201526704\" data-edps_ref=\"aa26704-15\">\n<nav class=\"toolbar\">\n\t<button class=\"toolbar-item\" id=\"metrics-siq\">Current usage metrics</button>\n\t<button class=\"toolbar-item\" id=\"info\">About article metrics</button>\n    \n\t\n\t<button class=\"toolbar-item\" id=\"return\">Return to article</button>\n</nav>\n\n<div class=\"panel\" data-for=\"metrics-siq\">\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"panel\" data-for=\"metrics-alm\"></div>\n\n<div class=\"panel\" data-for=\"info\">\n\t\n\n\t<p>Current usage metrics show cumulative count of Article Views (full-text article views including HTML views, PDF and ePub downloads, according to the available data)  and Abstracts Views on Vision4Press platform.</p>\n\n\t<p>Data correspond to usage on the plateform after 2015. XV. Assessing the achievability and precision of time-delay measurements", "authors": ["Bonvin, V.", "Tewes, M.", "Courbin, F.", "Kuntzer, T.", "Sluse, D.", "Meylan, G."], "author_address": ["AA(Laboratoire d'astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne (EPFL), Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290, Versoix, Switzerland), AB(Argelander-Institut f\u00fcr Astronomie, Auf dem H\u00fcgel 71, 53121, Bonn, Germany), AC(Laboratoire d'astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne (EPFL), Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290, Versoix, Switzerland), AD(Laboratoire d'astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne (EPFL), Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290, Versoix, Switzerland), AE(Institut d'Astrophysique et de G\u00e9ophysique, Universit\u00e9 de Li\u00e8ge, All\u00e9e du 6 Ao\u00fbt 17, B5c, 4000, Li\u00e8ge, Belgium), AF(Laboratoire d'astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne (EPFL), Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290, Versoix, Switzerland)"], "journal_name": "Astronomy and Astrophysics", "volume": "585", "publication_year": "2016/01/1", "start_page": "A88", "keywords": ["methods: data analysis", "gravitational lensing: strong", "cosmological parameters", "Astrophysics - Instrumentation and Methods for Astrophysics", "Astrophysics - Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics"], "url": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2016A&A...585A..88B", "abstract": "COSMOGRAIL is a long-term photometric monitoring of gravitationally lensed quasars aimed at implementing Refsdal's time-delay method to measure cosmological parameters, in particular H<SUB>0</SUB>. Given the long and well sampled light curves of strongly lensed quasars, time-delay measurements require numerical techniques whose quality must be assessed. To this end, and also in view of future monitoring programs or surveys such as the LSST, a blind signal processing competition named Time Delay Challenge 1 (TDC1) was held in 2014. The aim of the present paper, which is based on the simulated light curves from the TDC1, is double. First, we test the performance of the time-delay measurement techniques currently used in COSMOGRAIL. Second, we analyse the quantity and quality of the harvest of time delays obtained from the TDC1 simulations. To achieve these goals, we first discover time delays through a careful inspection of the light curves via a dedicated visual interface. Our measurement algorithms can then be applied to the data in an automated way. We show that our techniques have no significant biases, and yield adequate uncertainty estimates resulting in reduced \u03c7<SUP>2</SUP> values between 0.5 and 1.0. We provide estimates for the number and precision of time-delay measurements that can be expected from future time-delay monitoring campaigns as a function of the photometric signal-to-noise ratio and of the true time delay. We make our blind measurements on the TDC1 data publicly available.", "doi": "10.1051/0004-6361/201526704", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:1506.07524", "issn": "0004-6361"}, "Inspection status": "Complete"}
